UNESCO

Question

Asked by Lord Hylton

    To ask Her Majesty's Government what consultation, if any, they have had with UNESCO concerning past and current archaeological excavations within the Old City of Jerusalem; and whether they have made representations on those matters. [HL12767]

The Minister of State, Foreign and Commonwealth Office (Lord Howell of Guildford): The UK Government take an interest in the issue of archaeological excavations within the Old City and we support organisations that track such developments to make sure they reflect the sensitivity of such an historic site of importance to several religions. We are also closely following decisions over the possible demolition of the Mughrabi Gate bridge.

There are resolutions concerning archaeological excavations at the Old City of Jerusalem at each UNESCO Executive Board. However, the UK is not a member of this board and we have not had specific consultations with UNESCO concerning past or current excavations.

Vehicles: Semi-trailers

Questions

Asked by Lord Bradshaw

    To ask Her Majesty's Government, in their assessment of the impact of longer semi-trailers on safety, (a) what is the margin of error for the anticipated 1.6 per cent reduction in casualties estimated from assumptions on decreases in lorry miles, (b) what would be the impact on casualties if there is no decrease in lorry miles, and (c) what are the anticipated casualties in terms of (1) killed and seriously injured pedestrians, cyclists, car users, and other road users, and (2) minor injuries to pedestrians, cyclists, car users, and other road users.[HL12332]

Earl Attlee: The range of impacts around the 1.6 per cent figure is between zero and a reduction of 2.1 per cent.

The TRL report The likely effects of permitting longer semi-trailers in the UK: vehicle specification performance and safety considered the points at (b) and (c) and provided assessments where the potential impacts were identifiable.



1 Nov 2011 : Column WA258

A copy of the report is available from the Library of the House.

Asked by Lord Bradshaw

    To ask Her Majesty's Government, in their assessment of the impact of longer semi-trailers on safety, whether the present motorway speed limit of 70 miles per hour was used in the calculations; and what is their assessment of the combined anticipated effect on casualties of the increase in semi-trailers and the proposed 80 miles per hour motorway speed limit.[HL12333]

Earl Attlee: Current motorway speed limits were used in the impact assessment on longer semi-trailers.

The forthcoming consultation on raising the speed limit on motorways to 80 mph will include an impact assessment. The Government have no intention to raise the motorway speed limit for heavy goods vehicles.

Visas

Question

Asked by Lord Laird

    To ask Her Majesty's Government, further to the Written Answer by Lord Henley on 19 October (WA 78), how many confirmation of acceptance for studies visas were assigned in each of the last three years to Rayat London College and Lampton College in Hounslow; whether those colleges are trusted by the UK Border Agency; and whether they will review the position of the British Accreditation Council which accredited those colleges.[HL12719]

The Minister of State, Home Office (Lord Henley): Information on the number of confirmation of acceptance for studies (CAS) assigned since they were introduced on 22 February 2010 is as follows:

Sponsor22 February to December 2010January 2011 to 25 October 2011Total CAS Assigned

Rayat London College

123

433

556

Lampton College London

0

199

199

Neither college has highly trusted sponsor status.

The British Accreditation Council is no longer an approved accrediting body for tier 4 sponsors. In June 2011 new provisions were introduced requiring tier 4 sponsors to obtain educational oversight from one of the listed public bodies.

Question

The Minister of State, Foreign and Commonwealth Office (Lord Howell of Guildford): I refer the noble Lord to the answer by my noble friend Lord Wallace of Saltaire on 26 October 2011 (Official Report, col. WA170).
